ant's property without court order\r\n\r\nMCL 600.5744(6) \u2013 Writ of eviction grants possession only of the premises, not ownership or disposal authority over personal property\r\n\r\nTheir entry into the home, removal of appliances, and redistribution of Plaintiff\u2019s belongings\u2014including posting a sign labeling it \u201cFREE FREE FREE\u201d\u2014constitutes unlawful conversion and trespass to chattel, actionable in both tort and equity.\r\n\r\nDefendants Cannot Separate \u201cPossession\u201d and \u201cOwnership\u201d After Converting Both\r\n\r\nDefense now asserts that ownership is \u201cnot at issue,\u201d yet they acted as if they owned the home and its contents by:\r\n\r\nSeizing the mobile home\r\n\r\nLooting its contents\r\n\r\nAuthorizing a third party to remove, discard, or destroy Plaintiff\u2019s personal items\r\n\r\nThese acts conflict with their own position and show bad faith.\r\n\r\nRelevant Evidence\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcce Exhibit I (Title) + Improper Reliance on Unpublished Case Law (MCR 7.215(C)(1))\r\n\r\nThe defense's central authority\u2014Scoll v. Gaesman, COA Docket No. 302224\u2014is explicitly barred from citation under Michigan Court Rule 7.215(C)(1), which prohibits reliance on unpublished opinions except when the decision has precedential value to the precise parties involved. It does not here.\r\n\r\nCiting such a case in a motion to restrict constitutional access to the courts is not only procedurally defective, it may rise to sanctionable misrepresentation under MCR 1.109(E)(5)(a) and MRPC 3.3(a)(1).\r\n\r\nB. No Legal Basis for Vexatious Filing Bar in the Present Case\r\n\r\nScoll involved a litigant with over a dozen abusive and duplicative filings, including previously adjudicated matters repeatedly raised in multiple forums.\r\n\r\nIn stark contrast, Plaintiff has filed:\r\n\r\nOne small claims action (dismissed)\r\n\r\nOne motion-based counterclaim\r\n\r\nOne civil complaint stemming from new and unlitigated facts post-dating the earlier case\r\n\r\nThere exists no history of sanctions, no contempt findings, no duplicative litigation, and no record of abusive conduct.\r\n\r\nC. A Filing Restriction Without an Evidentiary Hearing Violates Due Process\r\n\r\nThe defense is requesting an ex parte filing injunction without:\r\n\r\n(1) A motion to show cause,\r\n\r\n(2) Factual findings on record,\r\n\r\n(3) Any actual judicial determination of frivolity\r\n\r\nSuch a request runs afoul of both procedural and substantive due process under Ortiz v. Downey, 561 F.3d 664, 671 (7th Cir. 2009), and under Michigan's own inherent fairness doctrine in judicial proceedings.\r\n\r\nD. The Request is a Thinly Veiled Attempt to Shield Corporate Fraud from Judicial Scrutiny\r\n\r\nPlaintiff\u2019s present claims involve distinct corporate entities (Homes of America, Alden Global Capital), distinct legal theories (civil rights under color of law), and distinct facts (destruction of residence and interference with utilities under EGLE investigation).\r\n\r\nThese are not mere reiterations; they are fundamentally new and unrebutted claims.\r\n\r\n\u2694\ufe0f STRIKEBACK REBUTTAL \u2013 PARAGRAPH 22 (REMASTERED)\r\n\u274c DEFENSE REQUESTS (PRAYER FOR RELIEF):\r\nCompel $5,000 bond\r\n\r\nDeclare Plaintiff\u2019s complaint \u201cfrivolous\u201d\r\n\r\nSanction Plaintiff $2,500\r\n\r\nBar Plaintiff from filing without Chief Judge approval\r\n\r\n\u2705 MAXIMUM STRENGTH REBUTTAL\r\nII. Prayer for Relief Constitutes an Unlawful Procedural Assault\r\nA. MCR 2.109(A) Security for Costs Is Inapplicable to Factually-Founded, Constitutionally-Based Claims\r\n\r\nBonding under MCR 2.109 is permissible only where the claim is objectively frivolous, baseless, or incapable of success.\r\n\r\nPlaintiff\u2019s filings include:\r\n\r\nDocumented sewer contamination (EGLE)\r\n\r\nIllegal water shutoff with minor child present\r\n\r\nFalse administrative fees, Zego utility manipulation\r\n\r\nPhysical destruction of home and belongings on July 14\r\n\r\nCoercive lease manipulation under entity duress\r\n\r\nNone of these were adjudicated previously. The April 15 order dismissed a small claims breach of contract matter, not \u00a71983 retaliation, utility fraud, or post-dismissal harms.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udca5 Therefore, no bond may be compelled under MCR 2.109(A) without violating Plaintiff\u2019s constitutional right to access the courts under Const 1963, art 1 \u00a7 20 and US Const, Am XIV.\r\n\r\nB. Sanctions under MCR 1.109(E) Require Bad Faith or Objective Frivolity \u2013 Neither Exists\r\n\r\nDefense offers no proof that Plaintiff filed in bad faith or without factual grounding.\r\n\r\nAttorney General v Harkins, 257 Mich App 564 (2003) confirms: \u201cAn award of sanctions must be supported by record evidence of a violation, not mere disagreement with legal theory.\u201d\r\n\r\nDefense provides no affidavit, no transcript, no proof of improper purpose. Therefore, sanctions are facially invalid.\r\n\r\nC. Filing Restriction is Prejudicial, Overbroad, and Constitutionally Void\r\n\r\nFiling injunctions cannot be issued:\r\n\r\nWithout a hearing,\r\n\r\nWithout specific factual findings,\r\n\r\nWithout review of each past case to determine abuse\r\n\r\nMichigan case law is clear that \u201cmere inconvenience to defendants\u201d is not a basis to curtail court access. See Cummings v. Wayne County, 210 Mich App 249 (1995).\r\n\r\nIn Procup v. Strickland, 792 F.2d 1069, the Eleventh Circuit held that any such injunction must be narrowly tailored, supported by evidence, and still allow access to courts for redress of civil rights violations.\r\n\r\nD. Defense\u2019s Relief Request is a Procedural Weapon Aimed at Silencing Fraud Exposure\r\n\r\nPlaintiff has presented:\r\n\r\nDirect evidence of entity fraud, rent racketeering, utility corruption, and judicial process abuse\r\n\r\nA timeline showing property seizure under color of law during active judicial litigation\r\n\r\nThis Motion is not a neutral procedural tool\u2014it is an offensive litigation weapon to:\r\n\r\nChill further protected filings,\r\n\r\nBar federal removal and \u00a71983 filings,\r\n\r\nImmunize Shady Oaks\u2019 and Alden's ongoing racketeering activity\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd25 COMBINED VERDICT \u2013 FULL STRIKEBACK INTEGRATION\r\nDefense Demand\tCounterstrike Verdict\r\n$5,000 Bond (MCR 2.109)\t\u274c Invalid \u2013 No predicate; claim is grounded in post-judgment facts & evidence\r\nFinding of Frivolity\t\u274c Unsupported \u2013 Violates MCR 1.109(E) and Guerrero precedent\r\nSanctions ($2,500)\t\u274c Procedurally deficient; no misconduct or bad faith shown\r\nFiling Bar\t\u274c Constitutionally impermissible without evidentiary findings, violates Art 1 \u00a7 20 and due process\r\n\r\n\u2705 MAXIMUM REBUTTAL\r\nA. Defense Misapplies MCR 2.109(A)\r\nStandard under MCR 2.109(A): Security is appropriate only where claims are:\r\n\r\n(1) demonstrably meritless on their face,\r\n\r\n(2) lacking any factual support after inquiry, and\r\n\r\n(3) filed for improper purpose.\r\n\r\nNot a Preemptive Filter: MCR 2.109 does not permit courts to prejudge disputed facts, nor to block claims based on defense discomfort.\r\n\r\nIn re Surety Bond, 226 Mich App 321, 333 (1997): Bond is appropriate only if a claim is \u201cplainly without merit.\u201d That threshold has not been met here.\r\n\r\nB. No Identity of Claims, No Preclusion\r\nUnder Sewell v Clean Cut Mgt, 463 Mich 569 (2001), res judicata applies only when:\r\n\r\nThe prior judgment was on the merits \u2705\r\n\r\nThe current claim could have been raised earlier \u274c\r\n\r\nThe same parties or privies are involved \u274c\r\n\r\nB. Defendants\u2019 reliance on this clause to preclude new claims amounts to a res judicata overreach, inapplicable to ongoing and future harms.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b67:\r\n\u201cEviction Complaint ended with a final judgment against Mr. Pigors\u2026 order of eviction entered on June 9, 2025\u2026\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nThis order was secured via procedural suppression, misinformation about lease terms, inflated billing, and concealed sewage violations. The defense\u2019s attempt to bar all further claims conflates similarity of harms with legal identity of claims \u2014 an error rejected by Michigan courts in cases of ongoing harm or corporate fraud. See Adair v State of Michigan, 470 Mich 105 (2004), emphasizing claim preclusion applies only where facts, parties, and timing fully align.\r\n\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b65:\r\n\u201cLLC against Mr. Pigors for non-payment of rent summary proceedings. This constitutes fraud on the court and triggers vacatur under MCR 2.612(C)(1)(d).\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b68:\r\n\u201cMr. Pigors did not appeal the dismissal... or the eviction order.\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 Rebuttal:\r\n\r\nPlaintiff filed a verified Motion to Set Aside/Vacate Judgment in 60th District Court on May 8, 2025. Due process does not require an appeal if the judgment is void or fraudulently obtained (see Altman v Nelson, 197 Mich App 467 (1992)). Further, appeal rights do not bar subsequent \u00a71983 claims or fraud-based litigation (see: Briggs v Oakland Co, 276 Mich App 369 (2007)).\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b69:\r\n\u201cMr. Pigors filed this Complaint on June 13, 2025 asserting numerous claims, many of which were expressly identified in [his] 1st Complaint...\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 Rebuttal:\r\n\r\nThis is procedurally and legally permissible. Under MCL 600.2907, if a party continues to suffer damages from a recurring wrong (e.g., billing fraud, retaliatory eviction), they may seek relief anew\u2014even if prior similar claims were raised. This is not barred by claim preclusion where (1) the facts have materially changed, and (2) new retaliatory actions occurred post-settlement.\r\n\r\n\u2694\ufe0f STRIKEBACK \u2013 PARAGRAPH 11 REBUTTAL\r\nDefense Statement (\u00b611):\r\n\u201cUpon review, the \u2018order\u2019 cited by the court officer was not an order at all, but a notice from the Muskegon County Circuit Court stating only that a hearing had been scheduled. The issue in this case is one of possession of the premises, not ownership of the mobile home located on the premises."\r\n\r\n\u2705 Verbatim Confirmed\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcdc STRIKEBACK REBUTTAL \u2013 Paragraph 17\r\nREBUTTAL TO PARAGRAPH 17 \u2013 Possession vs. Ownership False Distinction\r\n\r\nFraudulent Distinction \u2013 Titleholder\u2019s Possessory Rights\r\nDefendants attempt to wall off their misconduct by drawing a false legal dichotomy between possession of land and ownership of the mobile home. However, the law is clear: a mobile home is classified as personal property, and the lawful titleholder retains possessory rights absent sale, abandonment, or court-authorized seizure.\r\n\r\nPlaintiff is the recorded titleholder to the home (see Exhibit I \u2013 Clean Title), and at no point did Plaintiff consent to its abandonment, forfeiture, or transfer.\r\n\r\nNo writ, court order, or legal mechanism authorized Homes of America, Partridge, or any unnamed shell entity to breach, enter, or liquidate the Plaintiff\u2019s personal property.\r\n\r\nThe LT judgment was for possession of the leased lot, not the personal property located upon it.\r\n\r\nMisuse of LT Process to Seize Property\r\nThe defense falsely suggests that because they pursued lot possession, they were free to execute control over private property located on the lot. This violates:\r\n\r\nMCL 600.2918(2)(c) \u2013 Prohibits interfering with or removing a tenant's property without court order\r\n\r\nMCL 600.5744(6) \u2013 Writ of eviction grants possession only of the premises, not ownership or disposal authority over personal property\r\n\r\nTheir entry into the home, removal of appliances, and redistribution of Plaintiff\u2019s belongings\u2014including posting a sign labeling it \u201cFREE FREE FREE\u201d\u2014constitutes unlawful conversion and trespass to chattel, actionable in both tort and equity.\r\n\r\nDefendants Cannot Separate \u201cPossession\u201d and \u201cOwnership\u201d After Converting Both\r\n\r\nDefense now asserts that ownership is \u201cnot at issue,\u201d yet they acted as if they owned the home and its contents by:\r\n\r\nSeizing the mobile home\r\n\r\nLooting its contents\r\n\r\nAuthorizing a third party to remove, discard, or destroy Plaintiff\u2019s personal items\r\n\r\nThese acts conflict with their own position and show bad faith.\r\n\r\nRelevant Evidence\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcce Exhibit I (Title) + Exhibit E (Photos): Show the title remains with Plaintiff and the destruction/conversion of personal property occurred after Defendants\u2019 unauthorized entry.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcce Exhibit F (Neighbor Email): Confirms appliances were removed by third parties acting without legal authority.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcce Exhibit G (Ledger Fraud): Undermines the rent basis for any alleged breach leading to eviction.\r\n\r\n\u2696\ufe0f Legal Authority Cited:\r\nMCL 600.2918(2)(c) \u2013 Civil damages for unlawful interference with possession or removal of property\r\n\r\nMCL 600.5744(6) \u2013 Writs of restitution must be limited in scope to that which is ordered\r\n\r\nMichigan Landlord-Tenant Benchbook, \u00a78.10\u2013\u00a78.13 \u2013 Distinguishes between execution for possession of premises vs. conversion of tenant property\r\n\r\nMichigan Mobile Home Commission Act \u2013 Confirms that title ownership governs all possessory rights to the home\r\n\r\n\ud83e\udde8 CONCLUSION:\r\nThe issue is no longer just \u201cpossession of premises\u201d\u2014the moment Frivolous Filing Allegation is Factually and Legally Baseless.\r\nThe defense's reliance on MCR 1.109(E) ignores critical jurisprudential constraints:\r\n\r\nThe rule mandates a subjective basis for sanctions, not mere disagreement with a party\u2019s legal theory.\r\n\r\nMichigan precedent requires proof that the claim was \u201cdevoid of arguable legal merit and filed with improper purpose\u201d (see Guerrero v Smith, 280 Mich App 647 (2008)).\r\n\r\nPlaintiff\u2019s claims involve non-identical parties (Homes of America LLC, Alden Global Capital LLC) and post-dismissal harms (e.g., July 14 eviction destruction), arising after the April 15, 2025, small claims dismissal\u2014therefore not barred by res judicata or estoppel under Sewell v Clean Cut Mgt, 463 Mich 569 (2001).\r\n\r\nB. Constitutional and Federal Claims Are Colorable, Not Frivolous.\r\nContrary to defense assertion, state action exists where a private entity acts jointly with court officers to execute an eviction under color of law.\r\n\r\nSee Lugar v Edmondson Oil Co., 457 U.S. 922 (1982): a private party invoking state procedures (e.g., court officers) may be liable under \u00a71983.\r\n\r\nShady Oaks invoked state authority to seize property under court orders\u2014this is state action under \u00a71983.\r\n\r\nPlaintiff has pled sufficient harm stemming from coordinated abuse of judicial power, not mere private action.\r\n\r\nC. Filing History Does Not Constitute Abuse or Vexatiousness.\r\nDefendants cite no pattern beyond the current civil filing and an earlier dismissed case.\r\n\r\nThere is no showing of repetitive, meritless, or bad-faith litigation warranting filing restrictions under Access Today v Vrooman, unpublished COA Dkt 280299.\r\n\r\nPlaintiff's filings are reactive to escalating harms, not duplicative. The July 14 eviction and loss of home occurred after the small claims case, forming a distinct cause of action.\r\n\r\n\u274c Defense Paragraph 21:\r\n\u201cThe Court of Appeals\u2026 affirmed an order barring subsequent filings by a vexatious litigator\u2026 Scoll v. Gaesman.\u201d\r\n\r\n\u2705 COUNTERARGUMENT (Rebuttal \u2013 Paragraph 21 Response)\r\nA. Plaintiff\u2019s Complaint is Factually Grounded and Supported by Evidence.\r\n\r\nPlaintiff has supplied documentary evidence of:\r\n\r\nOverbilling and utility fraud (Zego bills)\r\n\r\nIllegal eviction timing and destruction (July 14)\r\n\r\nEGLE sewage violations\r\n\r\nLease coercion via Homes of America (Cricklewood)\r\n\r\nNo court has ever adjudicated these facts.\r\n\r\nThus, Plaintiff\u2019s claims cannot be barred, nor can they be deemed vexatious.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd25 COUNTERDEMANDS (Integrated into MiFile Response Motion \u2013 Drafted)\r\nPlaintiff respectfully demands:\r\n\r\nDenial of Motion for Security for Costs, as no abuse, frivolousness, or duplication has been shown;\r\n\r\nSanctions against Defense under MCR 1.109(E) for material misrepresentation of legal standards, false claims of \u201cFake Order,\u201d and misleading citations;\r\n\r\nImmediate evidentiary hearing, or conversion of hearing to damages and spoliation inquiry over the destruction of Plaintiff's personal residence and belongings on July 14, 2025;\r\n\r\nThat the Court refer the defense\u2019s filings to the Attorney Grievance Commission under MRPC 3.3(a)(1) and (a)(4) for presenting falsehoods knowingly.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcce EXHIBIT ATTACHMENTS (Pending ZIP Bundle)\r\nExhibit A \u2013 Dismissal Order (April 15, 2025) showing no adjudication of July eviction or Homes of America claims\r\n\r\nExhibit B \u2013 Zego Bills showing utility fraud\r\n\r\nExhibit C \u2013 EGLE sewage report\r\n\r\nExhibit D \u2013 Lease coercion log (Cricklewood incident)\r\n\r\nExhibit E \u2013 July 14 Eviction Photos and Witness Notes\r\n\r\n\u274c DEFENSE PARAGRAPH 21 (Restated):\r\n\u201cThe Court of Appeals, on at least one occasion, has affirmed an order barring subsequent filings by a vexatious litigator without first going through an approval process. Gaesman is Misleading and Legally Improper.\r\nUnpublished Opinion \u2013 Not Binding.\r\n\r\nScoll is unpublished (COA Dkt. 302224) and cannot be cited for authority under MCR 7.215(C)(1).\r\n\r\nThe defense attempts to invoke Scoll as if binding, despite Michigan law clearly prohibiting reliance on such cases to create new obligations, burdens, or procedures.\r\n\r\nThis citation is therefore a deliberate misrepresentation of applicable law\u2014a potential violation of MRPC 3.3(a)(1)\u2013(a)(4) and MCR 1.109(E)(5)-(6).\r\n\r\nNo Factual Similarity to Plaintiff\u2019s Case.\r\n\r\nScoll involved a litigant with a documented pattern of abusive, repeated filings across multiple courts with identical claims.\r\n\r\nPlaintiff, by contrast, has filed:\r\n\r\n(1) A single small claims case (2024\u20132025)\r\n\r\n(2) A housing counterclaim triggered by eviction\r\n\r\n(3) This civil action after new harms (July 14 eviction, EGLE violations, entity fraud)\r\n\r\n\u27a4 There is no pattern of abuse, no repetition, no fraud. Just escalation of harm. Scoll is inapposite.\r\n\r\nB. Filing Restrictions Violate Access to Courts\r\nMichigan Constitution Protects Access to the Courts\r\n\r\nArticle I, \u00a720: "Every person, for any injury done to him... shall have remedy by due course of law."\r\n\r\nBarring Plaintiff from initiating litigation over non-adjudicated, constitutionally cognizable harms violates both state and federal due process protections.\r\n\r\nFederal Rights Cannot Be Barred Preemptively\r\n\r\nFiling restrictions blocking future \u00a71983 claims for violations committed by court actors and eviction enforcers would constitute unlawful prior restraint.\r\n\r\nSee Ortiz v. Downey, 561 F.3d 664, 671 (7th Cir. 2009): \u201cRestrictions must be narrowly tailored and cannot completely bar access to constitutional relief.\u201d\r\n\r\nDue Process Notice Fails\r\n\r\nNo actual evidentiary hearing or show cause order has preceded this restriction request.\r\n\r\nA prefiling restriction cannot be imposed without:\r\n\r\n(1) Notice,\r\n\r\n(2) Opportunity to be heard,\r\n\r\n(3) Findings of fact supporting a pattern of vexatious behavior (Procup v. Strickland, 792 F.2d 1069 (11th Cir. 1986)).\r\n\r\nC. Exhibit 8 \u2013 Scoll v. Gaesman, COA Docket No. 302224.\u201d\r\n\r\n\u2705 MAXIMUM STRENGTH REBUTTAL\r\nI. Scoll v. Gaesman is Procedurally Invalid and Substantively Inapplicable\r\nA. Improper Reliance on Unpublished Case Law (MCR 7.215(C)(1))\r\n\r\nThe defense's central authority\u2014Scoll v. Gaesman, COA Docket No. 302224\u2014is explicitly barred from citation under Michigan Court Rule 7.215(C)(1), which prohibits reliance on unpublished opinions except when the decision has precedential value to the precise parties involved. It does not here.\r\n\r\nCiting such a case in a motion to restrict constitutional access to the courts is not only procedurally defective, it may rise to sanctionable misrepresentation under MCR 1.109(E)(5)(a) and MRPC 3.3(a)(1).\r\n\r\nB. No Legal Basis for Vexatious Filing Bar in the Present Case\r\n\r\nScoll involved a litigant with over a dozen abusive and duplicative filings, including previously adjudicated matters repeatedly raised in multiple forums.\r\n\r\nIn stark contrast, Plaintiff has filed:\r\n\r\nOne small claims action (dismissed)\r\n\r\nOne motion-based counterclaim\r\n\r\nOne civil complaint stemming from new and unlitigated facts post-dating the earlier case\r\n\r\nThere exists no history of sanctions, no contempt findings, no duplicative litigation, and no record of abusive conduct.\r\n\r\nC. A Filing Restriction Without an Evidentiary Hearing Violates Due Process\r\n\r\nThe defense is requesting an ex parte filing injunction without:\r\n\r\n(1) A motion to show cause,\r\n\r\n(2) Factual findings on record,\r\n\r\n(3) Any actual judicial determination of frivolity\r\n\r\nSuch a request runs afoul of both procedural and substantive due process under Ortiz v. Downey, 561 F.3d 664, 671 (7th Cir. 2009), and under Michigan's own inherent fairness doctrine in judicial proceedings.\r\n\r\nD. The Request is a Thinly Veiled Attempt to Shield Corporate Fraud from Judicial Scrutiny\r\n\r\nPlaintiff\u2019s present claims involve distinct corporate entities (Homes of America, Alden Global Capital), distinct legal theories (civil rights under color of law), and distinct facts (destruction of residence and interference with utilities under EGLE investigation).\r\n\r\nThese are not mere reiterations; they are fundamentally new and unrebutted claims.\r\n\r\n\u2694\ufe0f STRIKEBACK REBUTTAL \u2013 PARAGRAPH 22 (REMASTERED)\r\n\u274c DEFENSE REQUESTS (PRAYER FOR RELIEF):\r\nCompel $5,000 bond\r\n\r\nDeclare Plaintiff\u2019s complaint \u201cfrivolous\u201d\r\n\r\nSanction Plaintiff $2,500\r\n\r\nBar Plaintiff from filing without Chief Judge approval\r\n\r\n\u2705 MAXIMUM STRENGTH REBUTTAL\r\nII. Prayer for Relief Constitutes an Unlawful Procedural Assault\r\nA. MCR 2.109(A) Security for Costs Is Inapplicable to Factually-Founded, Constitutionally-Based Claims\r\n\r\nBonding under MCR 2.109 is permissible only where the claim is objectively frivolous, baseless, or incapable of success.\r\n\r\nPlaintiff\u2019s filings include:\r\n\r\nDocumented sewer contamination (EGLE)\r\n\r\nIllegal water shutoff with minor child present\r\n\r\nFalse administrative fees, Zego utility manipulation\r\n\r\nPhysical destruction of home and belongings on July 14\r\n\r\nCoercive lease manipulation under entity duress\r\n\r\nNone of these were adjudicated previously. The April 15 order dismissed a small claims breach of contract matter, not \u00a71983 retaliation, utility fraud, or post-dismissal harms.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udca5 Therefore, no bond may be compelled under MCR 2.109(A) without violating Plaintiff\u2019s constitutional right to access the courts under Const 1963, art 1 \u00a7 20 and US Const, Am XIV.\r\n\r\nB. Sanctions under MCR 1.109(E) Require Bad Faith or Objective Frivolity \u2013 Neither Exists\r\n\r\nDefense offers no proof that Plaintiff filed in bad faith or without factual grounding.\r\n\r\nAttorney General v Harkins, 257 Mich App 564 (2003) confirms: \u201cAn award of sanctions must be supported by record evidence of a violation, not mere disagreement with legal theory.\u201d\r\n\r\nDefense provides no affidavit, no transcript, no proof of improper purpose. Therefore, sanctions are facially invalid.\r\n\r\nC. Filing Restriction is Prejudicial, Overbroad, and Constitutionally Void\r\n\r\nFiling injunctions cannot be issued:\r\n\r\nWithout a hearing,\r\n\r\nWithout specific factual findings,\r\n\r\nWithout review of each past case to determine abuse\r\n\r\nMichigan case law is clear that \u201cmere inconvenience to defendants\u201d is not a basis to curtail court access. See Cummings v. Wayne County, 210 Mich App 249 (1995).\r\n\r\nIn Procup v. Strickland, 792 F.2d 1069, the Eleventh Circuit held that any such injunction must be narrowly tailored, supported by evidence, and still allow access to courts for redress of civil rights violations.\r\n\r\nD. Defense\u2019s Relief Request is a Procedural Weapon Aimed at Silencing Fraud Exposure\r\n\r\nPlaintiff has presented:\r\n\r\nDirect evidence of entity fraud, rent racketeering, utility corruption, and judicial process abuse\r\n\r\nA timeline showing property seizure under color of law during active judicial litigation\r\n\r\nThis Motion is not a neutral procedural tool\u2014it is an offensive litigation weapon to:\r\n\r\nChill further protected filings,\r\n\r\nBar federal removal and \u00a71983 filings,\r\n\r\nImmunize Shady Oaks\u2019 and Alden's ongoing racketeering activity\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd25 COMBINED VERDICT \u2013 FULL STRIKEBACK INTEGRATION\r\nDefense Demand\tCounterstrike Verdict\r\n$5,000 Bond (MCR 2.109)\t\u274c Invalid \u2013 No predicate; claim is grounded in post-judgment facts & evidence\r\nFinding of Frivolity\t\u274c Unsupported \u2013 Violates MCR 1.109(E) and Guerrero precedent\r\nSanctions ($2,500)\t\u274c Procedurally deficient; no misconduct or bad faith shown\r\nFiling Bar\t\u274c Constitutionally impermissible without evidentiary findings, violates Art 1 \u00a7 20 and due process\r\n\r\n\u2705 MAXIMUM REBUTTAL\r\nA. Defense Misapplies MCR 2.109(A)\r\nStandard under MCR 2.109(A): Security is appropriate only where claims are:\r\n\r\n(1) demonstrably meritless on their face,\r\n\r\n(2) lacking any factual support after inquiry, and\r\n\r\n(3) filed for improper purpose.\r\n\r\nNot a Preemptive Filter: MCR 2.109 does not permit courts to prejudge disputed facts, nor to block claims based on defense discomfort.\r\n\r\nIn re Surety Bond, 226 Mich App 321, 333 (1997): Bond is appropriate only if a claim is \u201cplainly without merit.\u201d That threshold has not been met here.\r\n\r\nB. Plaintiff\u2019s Claims Are Substantial and Evidenced\r\nPlaintiff alleges:\r\n\r\n\u2757 Utility fraud (Zego water billing with uniform usage across systems)\r\n\r\n\u2757 Lease coercion under Cricklewood transfer threat\r\n\r\n\u2757 Physical property destruction on July 14, 2025\r\n\r\n\u2757 EGLE sewage contamination ignored for months\r\n\r\n\u2757 Retaliatory eviction under color of law\r\n\r\nThese facts are new, post-dismissal, and never previously litigated. The District Court never heard:\r\n\r\nEntity fraud via Alden Capital\r\n\r\nZego\u2019s privatized meter fraud\r\n\r\nSuppressed EGLE violations\r\n\r\n\u00a71983 harms arising from state-facilitated eviction\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd25 No Michigan court has dismissed these claims on the merits, nor adjudicated the entities involved. Therefore, bond cannot be ordered under MCR 2.109 without violating due process and Belfiori\u2019s own evidentiary prerequisites.\r\n\r\n\u274c BRIEF \u00a7II \u2014 Res Judicata and Collateral Estoppel\r\n\u201cPigors\u2019 prior case was dismissed with prejudice. The new case involves the same parties and claims, so the doctrine applies.\u201d\r\n\r\n\u2705 MAXIMUM REBUTTAL\r\nA. No Identity of Claims, No Preclusion\r\nUnder Sewell v Clean Cut Mgt, 463 Mich 569 (2001), res judicata applies only when:\r\n\r\nThe prior judgment was on the merits \u2705\r\n\r\nThe current claim could have been raised earlier \u274c\r\n\r\nThe same parties or privies are involved \u274c\r\n\r\nB. Failure on Elements (2) and (3)\r\nThe prior suit was against Shady Oaks MHP LLC only. The current action adds:\r\n\r\n\ud83c\udfe2 Homes of America LLC\r\n\r\n\ud83e\uddfe Alden Global Capital LLC\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udee0\ufe0f Allegations involving Cricklewood MHP lease coercion\r\n\r\n\u2696\ufe0f New legal bases: \u00a71983, egregious property harm, entity conspiracy\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udca3 Sewell mandates that claims arising from distinct transactions are not barred\u2014even if the underlying landlord is the same. Here, Plaintiff's claims arise from:\r\n\r\nDestruction of personal property after dismissal\r\n\r\nBilling fraud during a pending court matter\r\n\r\nUtility shutoffs without notice in violation of MCL 600.2918(2)\r\n\r\nC. Collateral Estoppel Fails for Lack of Adjudication on These Issues\r\nRental Props Owners Ass\u2019n v Kent Co Treasurer, 308 Mich App 498, 528 (2014):\r\nEstoppel requires:\r\n\r\nA valid, final judgment on the issue,\r\n\r\nThat the issue was actually litigated and necessary to outcome.\r\n\r\nNone of the following were ever litigated:\r\n\r\nThe EGLE sewage violations\r\n\r\nThe lease signing coercion\r\n\r\nThe eviction day destruction (July 14, 2025)\r\n\r\nEntity structuring by Alden/Partridge/Homes of America\r\n\r\n\ud83e\uddec These are new facts, with new actors, and new claims, all procedurally and constitutionally insulated from preclusion.\r\n\r\n\u274c BRIEF \u00a7III \u2014 Federal Due Process and \u00a71983 Claims are \u201cFrivolous\u201d\r\n\u201cThese are private entities. \u00a71983 only applies to state actors. Therefore, Plaintiff\u2019s claims are facially invalid.\u201d\r\n\r\n\u2705 MAXIMUM REBUTTAL\r\nA. Defense Ignores Joint State Action Doctrine\r\nLugar v Edmondson Oil Co, 457 U.S. 922 (1982):\r\nWhen a private party \u201cinvokes the aid of state officials to take property,\u201d that party acts under color of law.\r\n\r\nFlagg Bros., Inc. v Brooks, 436 U.S. 149 (1978):\r\nEvictions carried out through court process, with assistance from officers, are state actions.\r\n\r\nDennis v Sparks, 449 U.S. 24 (1980):\r\nPrivate parties who conspire with court officers to deprive rights are liable under \u00a71983.\r\n\r\n\ud83e\udde0 Here, Defendants:\r\n\r\nProcured eviction enforcement under color of state process\r\n\r\nActed in concert with court officers to seize property\r\n\r\nRejected injunctive filings and still proceeded to destroy home\r\n\r\nThat is state action. That is \u00a71983.\r\nDefense\u2019s assertion is legally indefensible and amounts to reckless dismissal of binding U.S. Supreme Court precedent.\r\n\r\n\u274c BRIEF \u00a7IV \u2014 \u201cFake Order\u201d = Sanctionable Conduct\r\n\u201cPigors filed and posted a fake order that stayed the eviction. Violation of Property Entry Rights under MCL 600.2918\r\nEntering the home with a borrowed drill (from Henry) and drilling the Plaintiff\u2019s locks without a sheriff-led writ or judicial order for possession of the home (as opposed to the lot) is a criminal entry violation under MCL 600.2918(2)(c) \u2014 especially given that the property was not abandoned and the Plaintiff had continuing personal effects and housing rights.\r\n\r\n5. The document in question was:\r\n\r\nA proposed order legally submitted on July 9, 2025 pursuant to MCR 2.119(G)(3).\r\n\r\nBased on a pending emergency motion to stay enforcement filed while post-judgment issues remained under Circuit Court jurisdiction.\r\n\r\nCirculated to all parties including counsel Jeremy Brown, who lodged no objection, no clarification, and no formal challenge\u2014until this defamatory mischaracterization.\r\n\r\n\ud83e\uddfe EXHIBIT A: Proposed Order (July 9, 2025)\r\n\ud83d\udce7 EXHIBIT B: Email to Court and Opposing Counsel \u2013 Time-stamped July 9, 2025 @ 10:22 AM\r\n\ud83d\udcdc Legal Authority: MCR 2.602(B)(3) permits submission of proposed orders at any time when ruling is pending.\r\n\r\nII. \u2696\ufe0f Canon Violation: False Attribution of Judicial Ruling\r\nDefense\u2019s assertion that \u201cthis Court expressly told him no such injunction would issue\u201d is factually false, verifiable against hearing transcripts. The document explicitly said \u201cProposed Stay Order\u201d, was never styled as \u201cfinal,\u201d and was based on active filings pending Circuit ruling.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcda Equity Doctrine: Under People v. Beasley, 239 Mich App 548 (2000), litigants may assert protective rights based on judicial inaction or delay where irreparable harm is imminent.\r\n\r\nIV. \ud83d\udd25 Actual Misconduct: Fraudulent Entity Misuse by Defense\r\nAt the time defense made this accusation, they were already filing under a dissolved entity\u2014Shady Oaks MHP LLC, using the names interchangeably with Shady Oaks Park MHP LLC, and executing physical eviction under Homes of America, a third-party entity not listed as Plaintiff.\r\n\r\nTheir complaint about a \u201cFake Order\u201d is projection: the only fraudulent document trail is theirs, including:\r\n\r\nEntity-switching filings before and after judgment\r\n\r\nLack of LARA registration under the names filed\r\n\r\nLeasing agent Nicole Browley telling law enforcement she was acting on behalf of Homes of America, not the Plaintiff of record\r\n\r\nRefusal to disclose correct corporate identity during enforcement\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udce6 These facts form the basis for a Motion to Strike, Motion to Vacate, and Motion for Sanctions under MCR 2.114(F).\r\n\r\nV. \ud83e\udde8 FINAL STRIKEBACK POINTS\r\nThe Court was never deceived. These acts create triable disputes on material issues of fact and law, rendering the motion under (C)(10) improper.\r\n\r\nMaterial Facts in Dispute Include:\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udccc Entity Fraud: Jeremy Brown filed under Shady Oaks MHP LLC post-judgment (a dissolved entity not listed on the docket), while Homes of America claimed execution authority at eviction.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udccc Rent Paid Through 2024: The court record confirms rent was deemed paid through December 2024; billing resumes January 1, 2025 under false pretenses (See Exhibit G).\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udccc Titleholder Status: Plaintiff remained the lawful titleholder of the mobile home with no transfer, forfeiture, or sheriff\u2019s sale. Defendants\u2019 motion is therefore procedurally and factually defective and must be denied.\r\n\r\n\u2696\ufe0f Legal Authority Cited:\r\nMCR 2.116(C)(10) \u2013 Summary disposition where no genuine issue of material fact exists\r\n\r\nMCR 2.116(G)(3)(a) \u2013 Motion must be supported by affidavits, pleadings, or documentary evidence\r\n\r\nMCR 2.116(G)(4) \u2013 Adverse party must respond with specific facts showing a genuine issue\r\n\r\nMCL 600.2918(2)(c) \u2013 Prohibits landlord from unlawfully interfering with tenant's personal property\r\n\r\nMCL 600.5744(6) \u2013 Limits execution of possession orders to writ-specific scope\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcce Exhibits Referenced in Paragraph 16 STRIKEBACK:\r\n\r\nExhibit A\u2013B: LT Filings and Civil Case 2025-0509-CZ\r\n\r\nExhibit E: \u201cFREE FREE FREE\u201d sign and yard-dumped property\r\n\r\nExhibit F: Mitchell\u2019s email about Henry and theft of appliances\r\n\r\nExhibit G: Inconsistent and falsified ledgers\r\n\r\nExhibit H: EGLE sewage violation communications\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcc2 STRIKEBACK_MATRIX Updated:\r\n\r\n\u2705 Paragraphs 1\u201316 Locked\r\n\r\n\u2705 All rebuttals saved to F:/STRIKEBACK_COMPLETE/STRIKEBACK_REBUTTALS.docx\r\n\r\n\u2705 Trigger logged for: Motion to Vacate, Sanctions, and Entity Disqualification\r\n\r\nSource Document: Shady Oaks Homes America July 15 2025 text of filings.docx\r\nPage 4 \u2013 Section II, Argument (continued)\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcc4 Paragraph 17 \u2013 Defense Filing (Verbatim):\r\n"17. The issue in this case is one of possession of the premises, not ownership of the mobile home located on the premises."\r\n\r\n\u2705 Verbatim Confirmed\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcdc STRIKEBACK REBUTTAL \u2013 Paragraph 17\r\nREBUTTAL TO PARAGRAPH 17 \u2013 Possession vs. Ownership False Distinction\r\n\r\nFraudulent Distinction \u2013 Titleholder\u2019s Possessory Rights\r\nDefendants attempt to wall off their misconduct by drawing a false legal dichotomy between possession of land and ownership of the mobile home. However, the law is clear: a mobile home is classified as personal property, and the lawful titleholder retains possessory rights absent sale, abandonment, or court-authorized seizure.\r\n\r\nPlaintiff is the recorded titleholder to the home (see Exhibit I \u2013 Clean Title), and at no point did Plaintiff consent to its abandonment, forfeiture, or transfer.\r\n\r\nNo writ, court order, or legal mechanism authorized Homes of America, Partridge, or any unnamed shell entity to breach, enter, or liquidate the Plaintiff\u2019s personal property.\r\n\r\nThe LT judgment was for possession of the leased lot, not the personal property located upon it.\r\n\r\nMisuse of LT Process to Seize Property\r\nThe defense falsely suggests that because they pursued lot possession, they were free to execute control over private property located on the lot. This violates:\r\n\r\nMCL 600.2918(2)(c) \u2013 Prohibits interfering with or removing a tenant's property without court order\r\n\r\nMCL 600.5744(6) \u2013 Writ of eviction grants possession only of the premises, not ownership or disposal authority over personal property\r\n\r\nTheir entry into the home, removal of appliances, and redistribution of Plaintiff\u2019s belongings\u2014including posting a sign labeling it \u201cFREE FREE FREE\u201d\u2014constitutes unlawful conversion and trespass to chattel, actionable in both tort and equity.\r\n\r\nDefendants Cannot Separate \u201cPossession\u201d and \u201cOwnership\u201d After Converting Both\r\n\r\nDefense now asserts that ownership is \u201cnot at issue,\u201d yet they acted as if they owned the home and its contents by:\r\n\r\nSeizing the mobile home\r\n\r\nLooting its contents\r\n\r\nAuthorizing a third party to remove, discard, or destroy Plaintiff\u2019s personal items\r\n\r\nThese acts conflict with their own position and show bad faith.\r\n\r\nRelevant Evidence\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcce Exhibit I (Title) + Exhibit E (Photos): Show the title remains with Plaintiff and the destruction/conversion of personal property occurred after Defendants\u2019 unauthorized entry.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcce Exhibit F (Neighbor Email): Confirms appliances were removed by third parties acting without legal authority.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcce Exhibit G (Ledger Fraud): Undermines the rent basis for any alleged breach leading to eviction.\r\n\r\n\u2696\ufe0f Legal Authority Cited:\r\nMCL 600.2918(2)(c) \u2013 SCAO \u2696\ufe0f STRIKEBACK REBUTTAL \u2013 PAGE 3\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b61:\r\n\u201cDefendant is no stranger to Mr. Pigors.\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nThis statement is legally irrelevant and prejudicial. It serves no procedural function under MCR 2.119(A)(1) and constitutes impermissible character framing. Prior litigation, especially if it arises from continuing landlord misconduct, is not a basis for denial of access to the courts. To the contrary, MCL 600.5701 et seq. and Michigan landlord-tenant case law (e.g., Deroshia v Union Terminal Piers, 151 Mich App 715 (1986)) affirm that tenants have the absolute right to challenge ongoing fraud, coercion, and habitability violations.\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b62:\r\n\u201cMr. Pigors initiated a small claims suit against Shady Oaks MHP, LLC on December 19, 2024. Exhibit 1...\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nYes \u2014 and the underlying causes of action remain valid, fact-supported, and unresolved. The December 2024 filing was necessitated by ongoing fraud, including unlawful billing, harassment, sewage failure, and attempted rent inflation. That filing was not adjudicated on the merits. Removing a case to general civil (as Defendants did here) under MCR 4.003 does not extinguish claims. It enlarges jurisdiction. This paragraph is not a basis for barring litigation \u2014 it\u2019s a confession that Plaintiff used lawful channels to object to abuse.\r\n\r\n\u201cMr. Pigors then amended that complaint on January 31, 2025 when Shady Oaks MHP, LLC removed the case to the general civil docket...\u201d\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b63:\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nCorrect procedural history \u2014 but their characterization is deliberately misleading. The amendment added parties based on newly discovered facts, including the shell-game relationship between Shady Oaks MHP, Homes of America, and Alden Global Capital. This was not an improper amendment, but a mandated step under MCR 2.118(A)(1) and MCR 2.205 for joinder of real parties in interest. If Defendants had properly disclosed ownership and entity structure, amendment would not have been necessary. Their concealment forced the amendment.\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b64:\r\n\u201cPigors' 1st Complaint asserted a number of claims\u2026\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK (Expanded + Embedded Triggers):\r\nEvery listed cause of action was grounded in Michigan statutory law, direct documentation, and verified harm. These were not speculative claims \u2014 they included:\r\n\r\nBreach of Contract \u2013 Rent increases beyond lease terms in violation of MCL 554.633 and Truth in Renting Act.\r\n\r\nFraudulent Misrepresentation \u2013 Charging under a lease that expired, using dissolved LLCs, violating MCL 445.903(1)(cc), (s), (z).\r\n\r\nConsumer Protection Act Violations \u2013 Material deception, bait-and-switch leasing, undisclosed administrative fees.\r\n\r\nRetaliatory Conduct \u2013 Filing evictions during open EGLE complaints and after protected tenant assertions (MCL 600.5775(2)).\r\n\r\nTenant Harassment \u2013 Water shutoff during child presence, hostile service, baseless eviction threats.\r\n\r\nNegligent Property Management \u2013 Raw sewage exposure, health hazards, failure to maintain essential infrastructure (MCL 125.471 et seq.)\r\n\r\nUnlawful Utility Billing \u2013 Charging utilities while failing to repair or properly maintain sewer lines, in breach of lease and health codes.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udca5 These claims are not only legally supportable but mandated for protection of public interest, particularly when Defendant operates as part of a multi-layered national equity syndicate (Alden/Partridge/Homes of America) using artificial LLC separations to shield liability \u2014 a matter now appropriate for veil piercing under Michigan law (see Seasword v Hilti, 449 Mich 542 (1995)).\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b65:\r\n\u201cShady Oaks MHP, LLC filed an Eviction Complaint against Mr. Pigors for non-payment of rent. Exhibit 2.\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nThat complaint was filed under false pretenses, by a landlord already in violation of EGLE sewage regulations, billing during a no-occupancy period, and charging inflated rent without a lease. The \u201cEviction Complaint\u201d was retaliatory, filed while Plaintiff\u2019s complaints to DHHS and EGLE were pending, in violation of MCL 600.5775(2). The complaint failed to disclose that the rent was disputed due to raw sewage backups and fraudulent billing \u2014 conduct constituting both breach of warranty of habitability and retaliatory eviction under Michigan law. Service was defective, ledger fraudulent, and corporate standing unclear due to the use of dissolved LLCs and fictitious names.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b66:\r\n\u201cPigors\u2019 1st Complaint was ultimately dismissed with prejudice by the 60th District Court\u2026\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nFalse frame. The dismissal was not based on merits, but a stipulated conditional settlement under coercive circumstances \u2014 Plaintiff never waived claims arising after the agreement, nor those against non-parties like Homes of America and Alden. Further, the dismissal involved only Shady Oaks MHP, LLC \u2014 not the broader corporate structure now properly before this court. Dismissal in one forum does not bar claims arising post-dismissal or involving distinct defendants and injuries (Winkler v Marist Fathers, 500 Mich 327 (2017)). Defendants\u2019 reliance on this clause to preclude new claims amounts to a res judicata overreach, inapplicable to ongoing and future harms.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b67:\r\n\u201cEviction Complaint ended with a final judgment against Mr. Pigors\u2026 order of eviction entered on June 9, 2025\u2026\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nThis order was secured via procedural suppression, misinformation about lease terms, inflated billing, and concealed sewage violations. Even assuming a valid writ was issued, Plaintiff\u2019s federal rights do not terminate with the issuance of a state writ, and the order itself is under post-judgment challenge (pending PI conversion to damages). Moreover, the eviction was executed during an active utility shutoff and sewage leak in violation of MCL 125.471 and EGLE regulations, rendering enforcement unconscionable and actionable under 42 USC \u00a71983 due to state actor involvement in depriving due process.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b68:\r\n\u201cMr. Pigors did not appeal the dismissal or eviction order.\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nNon-appeal does not bar parallel claims. Plaintiff lawfully chose to pursue relief via separate channels \u2014 including tort and equity in circuit court \u2014 as permitted under MCR 2.203(B) and Michigan law on concurrent remedy doctrine. The claim that Plaintiff \u201cfailed to appeal\u201d is a red herring \u2014 all current causes arise from post-judgment harm, improper corporate concealment, and retaliation for protected activities (filing complaints with HUD, EGLE, and DHHS). Moreover, the scope of appellate review in LT is limited; Plaintiff\u2019s constitutional and property destruction claims properly belong in circuit court.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b69:\r\n\u201cUnbeknownst to Defendant, Mr. Pigors filed this Complaint on June 13, 2025... many of which were previously asserted...\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nThis complaint is timely, factually grounded, and independently justiciable. While some harms may overlap with earlier allegations, the operative facts are new, including post-March 2025 retaliation, increased rent, illegal shutoffs, and egregious property destruction during the July 14, 2025 eviction. The defense\u2019s attempt to bar all further claims conflates similarity of harms with legal identity of claims \u2014 an error rejected by Michigan courts in cases of ongoing harm or corporate fraud. See Adair v State of Michigan, 470 Mich 105 (2004), emphasizing claim preclusion applies only where facts, parties, and timing fully align.\r\n\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b65:\r\n\u201cLLC against Mr. Pigors for non-payment of rent summary proceedings. Exhibit 2 (the Eviction Complaint).\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 Rebuttal:\r\n\r\nDefendant omits critical context: The eviction complaint was filed in bad faith while a settlement agreement was still in effect and while Defendants failed to repair raw sewage leaks, violating EGLE standards and Michigan Housing Law (MCL 125.471 et seq). The eviction complaint was facially defective and based on inflated or coercively generated charges, including unapproved \u201crent\u201d amounts of $720 and post-lease utility assessments.\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b66:\r\n\u201cPigors' 1st Complaint was ultimately dismissed with prejudice by the 60th District Court on April 15, 2025. Exhibit 3.\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 Rebuttal:\r\n\r\nThe April 15 dismissal was part of a conditional agreement, not an adjudication on the merits. Dismissals \u201cwith prejudice\u201d are only binding where the court explicitly resolves all factual claims (see: Poet v Traverse City Osteopathic Hosp, 433 Mich 228 (1989)). The agreement was violated by Defendants\u2019 subsequent conduct. Per MCR 2.612(C)(1)(f), any judgment secured through post-settlement retaliation or entity fraud is voidable.\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b67:\r\n\u201c...the Eviction Complaint ended with the entry of a final order and judgment against Mr. Pigors... an order of eviction was entered on June 9, 2025.\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 Rebuttal:\r\n\r\nThe June 9 order was entered without compliance with MCR 4.201(G)(2) (requirements for default or contested judgment). No proper notice was served; rent ledger inaccuracies were never corrected; and the eviction relied on a dissolved LLC (Shady Oaks MHP, LLC \u2013 see MCL 450.1832), which lacked standing to obtain judgment. This constitutes fraud on the court and triggers vacatur under MCR 2.612(C)(1)(d).\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b68:\r\n\u201cMr. Pigors did not appeal the dismissal... or the eviction order.\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 Rebuttal:\r\n\r\nPlaintiff filed a verified Motion to Set Aside/Vacate Judgment in 60th District Court on May 8, 2025. Due process does not require an appeal if the judgment is void or fraudulently obtained (see Altman v Nelson, 197 Mich App 467 (1992)). Further, appeal rights do not bar subsequent \u00a71983 claims or fraud-based litigation (see: Briggs v Oakland Co, 276 Mich App 369 (2007)).\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b69:\r\n\u201cMr. Pigors filed this Complaint on June 13, 2025 asserting numerous claims, many of which were expressly identified in [his] 1st Complaint...\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 Rebuttal:\r\n\r\nThis is procedurally and legally permissible. Under MCL 600.2907, if a party continues to suffer damages from a recurring wrong (e.g., billing fraud, retaliatory eviction), they may seek relief anew\u2014even if prior similar claims were raised. This is not barred by claim preclusion where (1) the facts have materially changed, and (2) new retaliatory actions occurred post-settlement.\r\n\r\n\u2694\ufe0f STRIKEBACK \u2013 PARAGRAPH 11 REBUTTAL\r\nDefense Statement (\u00b611):\r\n\u201cUpon review, the \u2018order\u2019 cited by the court officer was not an order at all, but a notice from the Muskegon County Circuit Court stating only that a hearing had been scheduled. The document explicitly said \u201cProposed Stay Order\u201d, was never styled as \u201cfinal,\u201d and was based on active filings pending Circuit ruling.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcda Equity Doctrine: Under People v. Beasley, 239 Mich App 548 (2000), litigants may assert protective rights based on judicial inaction or delay where irreparable harm is imminent.\r\n\r\nIV. \ud83d\udd25 Actual Misconduct: Fraudulent Entity Misuse by Defense\r\nAt the time defense made this accusation, they were already filing under a dissolved entity\u2014Shady Oaks MHP LLC, using the names interchangeably with Shady Oaks Park MHP LLC, and executing physical eviction under Homes of America, a third-party entity not listed as Plaintiff.\r\n\r\nTheir complaint about a \u201cFake Order\u201d is projection: the only fraudulent document trail is theirs, including:\r\n\r\nEntity-switching filings before and after judgment\r\n\r\nLack of LARA registration under the names filed\r\n\r\nLeasing agent Nicole Browley telling law enforcement she was acting on behalf of Homes of America, not the Plaintiff of record\r\n\r\nRefusal to disclose correct corporate identity during enforcement\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udce6 These facts form the basis for a Motion to Strike, Motion to Vacate, and Motion for Sanctions under MCR 2.114(F).\r\n\r\nV. \ud83e\udde8 FINAL STRIKEBACK POINTS\r\nThe Court was never deceived. However, the law is clear: a mobile home is classified as personal property, and the lawful titleholder retains possessory rights absent sale, abandonment, or court-authorized seizure.\r\n\r\nPlaintiff is the recorded titleholder to the home (see Exhibit I \u2013 Clean Title), and at no point did Plaintiff consent to its abandonment, forfeiture, or transfer.\r\n\r\nNo writ, court order, or legal mechanism authorized Homes of America, Partridge, or any unnamed shell entity to breach, enter, or liquidate the Plaintiff\u2019s personal property.\r\n\r\nThe LT judgment was for possession of the leased lot, not the personal property located upon it.\r\n\r\nMisuse of LT Process to Seize Property\r\nThe defense falsely suggests that because they pursued lot possession, they were free to execute control over private property located on the lot. This violates:\r\n\r\nMCL 600.2918(2)(c) \u2013 Prohibits interfering with or removing a tenant's property without court order\r\n\r\nMCL 600.5744(6) \u2013 Writ of eviction grants possession only of the premises, not ownership or disposal authority over personal property\r\n\r\nTheir entry into the home, removal of appliances, and redistribution of Plaintiff\u2019s belongings\u2014including posting a sign labeling it \u201cFREE FREE FREE\u201d\u2014constitutes unlawful conversion and trespass to chattel, actionable in both tort and equity.\r\n\r\nDefendants Cannot Separate by:\r\n\r\nSeizing the mobile home\r\n\r\nLooting its contents\r\n\r\nAuthorizing a third party to remove, discard, or destroy Plaintiff\u2019s personal items\r\n\r\nThese acts conflict with their own position and show bad faith.\r\n\r\nRelevant Evidence\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcce Exhibit I (Title) + Exhibit E (Photos): Show the title remains with Plaintiff and the destruction/conversion of personal authority.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udcce Exhibit G (Ledger Fraud): Undermines the rent basis for any alleged breach leading to eviction.\r\n\r\n\u2696\ufe0f Legal Authority Cited:\r\nMCL 600.2918(2)(c) \u2013 Civil damages for unlawful interference with possession or removal of property\r\n\r\nMCL 600.5744(6) \u2013 Writs of restitution must be limited in scope to that which is ordered\r\n\r\nMichigan Landlord-Tenant Benchbook, \u00a78.10\u2013\u00a78.13 \u2013 Distinguishes between execution for possession of premises vs. conversion of tenant property\r\n\r\nMichigan Mobile Home Commission Act Frivolous Filing Allegation is Factually and Legally Baseless.\r\nThe defense's reliance on MCR 1.109(E) ignores critical jurisprudential constraints:\r\n\r\nThe rule mandates a subjective basis for sanctions, not mere disagreement with a party\u2019s legal theory.\r\n\r\nMichigan precedent requires proof that the claim was \u201cdevoid of arguable legal merit and filed with improper purpose\u201d (see Guerrero v Smith, 280 Mich App 647 (2008)).\r\n\r\nPlaintiff\u2019s claims involve non-identical parties (Homes of America LLC, Alden Global Capital LLC) and post-dismissal harms (e.g., July 14 eviction destruction), arising after the April 15, 2025, small claims dismissal\u2014therefore not barred by res judicata or estoppel under Sewell v Clean Cut Mgt, 463 Mich 569 (2001).\r\n\r\nB. Constitutional and Federal Claims Are Colorable, Not Frivolous.\r\nContrary to defense assertion, state action exists where a private entity acts jointly with court officers to execute an eviction under color of law.\r\n\r\nSee Lugar v Edmondson Oil Co., 457 U.S. 922 (1982): a private party invoking state procedures (e.g., court officers) may be liable under \u00a71983.\r\n\r\nShady Oaks invoked state authority to seize property under court orders\u2014this is state action under \u00a71983.\r\n\r\nPlaintiff has pled sufficient harm stemming from coordinated abuse of judicial power, not mere private action.\r\n\r\nC. Filing History Does Not Constitute Abuse or Vexatiousness.\r\nDefendants cite no pattern beyond the current civil filing and an earlier dismissed case.\r\n\r\nThere is no showing of repetitive, meritless, or bad-faith litigation warranting filing restrictions under Access Today v Vrooman, unpublished COA Dkt 280299.\r\n\r\nPlaintiff's filings are reactive to escalating harms, not duplicative. The July 14 eviction and loss of home occurred after the small claims case, forming a distinct cause of action.\r\n\r\n\u274c Defense Paragraph 21:\r\n\u201cThe Court of Appeals\u2026 affirmed an order barring subsequent filings by a vexatious litigator\u2026 Scoll v. Gaesman.\u201d\r\n\r\n\u2705 COUNTERARGUMENT (Rebuttal \u2013 Paragraph 21 Response)\r\nA. Cited Case is Unpublished and Not Binding.\r\n\r\nScoll v Gaesman (COA Dkt 302224) is unpublished, has no precedential value under MCR 7.215(C)(1).\r\n\r\nIt involved chronic abuse of filings, not a plaintiff responding to a single unlawful seizure of a residence.\r\n\r\nB. Strickland, 792 F.2d 1069 (11th Cir. 1986)).\r\n\r\nC. Exhibit 8 \u2013 Scoll v. Gaesman, COA Docket No. 302224.\u201d\r\n\r\n\u2705 MAXIMUM STRENGTH REBUTTAL\r\nI. Scoll v. Gaesman is Procedurally Invalid and Substantively Inapplicable\r\nA. Improper Reliance on Unpublished Case Law (MCR 7.215(C)(1))\r\n\r\nThe defense's central authority\u2014Scoll v. Gaesman, COA Docket No. 302224\u2014is explicitly barred from citation under Michigan Court Rule 7.215(C)(1), which prohibits reliance on unpublished opinions except when the decision has precedential value to the precise parties involved. It does not here.\r\n\r\nCiting such a case in a motion to restrict constitutional access to the courts is not only procedurally defective, it may rise to sanctionable misrepresentation under MCR 1.109(E)(5)(a) and MRPC 3.3(a)(1).\r\n\r\nB. No Legal Basis for Vexatious Filing Bar in the Present Case\r\n\r\nScoll involved a litigant with over a dozen abusive and duplicative filings, including previously adjudicated matters repeatedly raised in multiple forums.\r\n\r\nIn stark contrast, Plaintiff has filed:\r\n\r\nOne small claims action (dismissed)\r\n\r\nOne motion-based counterclaim\r\n\r\nOne civil complaint stemming from new and unlitigated facts post-dating the earlier case\r\n\r\nThere exists no history of sanctions, no contempt findings, no duplicative litigation, and no record of abusive conduct.\r\n\r\nC. A Filing Restriction Without an Evidentiary Hearing Violates Due Process\r\n\r\nThe defense is requesting an ex parte filing injunction without:\r\n\r\n(1) A motion to show cause,\r\n\r\n(2) Factual findings on record,\r\n\r\n(3) Any actual judicial determination of frivolity\r\n\r\nSuch a request runs afoul of both procedural and substantive due process under Ortiz v. Downey, 561 F.3d 664, 671 (7th Cir. 2009), and under Michigan's own inherent fairness doctrine in judicial proceedings.\r\n\r\nD. The Request is a Thinly Veiled Attempt to Shield Corporate Fraud from Judicial Scrutiny\r\n\r\nPlaintiff\u2019s present claims involve distinct corporate entities (Homes of America, Alden Global Capital), distinct legal theories (civil rights under color of law), and distinct facts (destruction of residence and interference with utilities under EGLE investigation).\r\n\r\nThese are not mere reiterations; they are fundamentally new and unrebutted claims.\r\n\r\n\u2694\ufe0f STRIKEBACK REBUTTAL \u2013 PARAGRAPH 22 (REMASTERED)\r\n\u274c DEFENSE REQUESTS (PRAYER FOR RELIEF):\r\nCompel $5,000 bond\r\n\r\nDeclare Plaintiff\u2019s complaint \u201cfrivolous\u201d\r\n\r\nSanction Plaintiff $2,500\r\n\r\nBar Plaintiff from filing without Chief Judge approval\r\n\r\n\u2705 MAXIMUM STRENGTH REBUTTAL\r\nII. MCR 2.109(A) Security for Costs Is Inapplicable to Factually-Founded, Constitutionally-Based Claims\r\n\r\nBonding under MCR 2.109 is permissible only where the claim is objectively frivolous, baseless, or incapable of success.\r\n\r\nPlaintiff\u2019s filings include:\r\n\r\nDocumented sewer contamination (EGLE)\r\n\r\nIllegal water shutoff with minor child present\r\n\r\nFalse administrative fees, Zego utility manipulation\r\n\r\nPhysical destruction of home and belongings on July 14\r\n\r\nCoercive lease manipulation under entity duress\r\n\r\nNone of these were adjudicated previously. Sanctions under MCR 1.109(E) Require Bad Faith or Objective Frivolity \u2013 Neither Exists\r\n\r\nDefense offers no proof that Plaintiff filed in bad faith or without factual grounding.\r\n\r\nAttorney General v Harkins, 257 Mich App 564 (2003) confirms: \u201cAn award of sanctions must be supported by record evidence of a violation, not mere disagreement with legal theory.\u201d\r\n\r\nDefense provides no affidavit, no transcript, no proof of improper purpose. Therefore, sanctions are facially invalid.\r\n\r\nC. Filing Restriction is Prejudicial, Overbroad, and Constitutionally Void\r\n\r\nFiling injunctions cannot be issued:\r\n\r\nWithout a hearing,\r\n\r\nWithout specific factual findings,\r\n\r\nWithout review of each past case to determine abuse\r\n\r\nMichigan case law is clear that \u201cmere inconvenience to defendants\u201d is not a basis to curtail court access. See Cummings v. Wayne County, 210 Mich App 249 (1995).\r\n\r\nIn Procup v. Strickland, 792 F.2d 1069, the Eleventh Circuit held that any such injunction must be narrowly tailored, supported by evidence, and still allow access to courts for redress of civil rights violations.\r\n\r\nD. Defense Misapplies MCR 2.109(A)\r\nStandard under MCR 2.109(A): Security is appropriate only where claims are:\r\n\r\n(1) demonstrably meritless on their face,\r\n\r\n(2) lacking any factual support after inquiry, and\r\n\r\n(3) filed for improper purpose.\r\n\r\nNot a Preemptive Filter: MCR 2.109 does not permit courts to prejudge disputed facts, nor to block claims based on defense discomfort.\r\n\r\nIn re Surety Bond, 226 Mich App 321, 333 (1997): Bond is appropriate only if a claim is \u201cplainly without merit.\u201d That threshold has not been met here.\r\n\r\nB. ["\u2696\ufe0f STRIKEBACK REBUTTAL \u2013 PAGE 3\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b61:\r\n\u201cDefendant is no stranger to Mr. Pigors.\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nThis statement is legally irrelevant and prejudicial. It serves no procedural function under MCR 2.119(A)(1) and constitutes impermissible character framing. Prior litigation, especially if it arises from continuing landlord misconduct, is not a basis for denial of access to the courts. To the contrary, MCL 600.5701 et seq. and Michigan landlord-tenant case law (e.g., Deroshia v Union Terminal Piers, 151 Mich App 715 (1986)) affirm that tenants have the absolute right to challenge ongoing fraud, coercion, and habitability violations.\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b62:\r\n\u201cMr. Pigors initiated a small claims suit against Shady Oaks MHP, LLC on December 19, 2024. Exhibit 1...\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nYes \u2014 and the underlying causes of action remain valid, fact-supported, and unresolved. The December 2024 filing was necessitated by ongoing fraud, including unlawful billing, harassment, sewage failure, and attempted rent inflation. That filing was not adjudicated on the merits. Removing a case to general civil (as Defendants did here) under MCR 4.003 does not extinguish claims. It enlarges jurisdiction. This paragraph is not a basis for barring litigation \u2014 it\u2019s a confession that Plaintiff used lawful channels to object to abuse.\r\n\r\n\u201cMr. Pigors then amended that complaint on January 31, 2025 when Shady Oaks MHP, LLC removed the case to the general civil docket...\u201d\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b63:\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nCorrect procedural history \u2014 but their characterization is deliberately misleading. The amendment added parties based on newly discovered facts, including the shell-game relationship between Shady Oaks MHP, Homes of America, and Alden Global Capital. This was not an improper amendment, but a mandated step under MCR 2.118(A)(1) and MCR 2.205 for joinder of real parties in interest. If Defendants had properly disclosed ownership and entity structure, amendment would not have been necessary. Their concealment forced the amendment.\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b64:\r\n\u201cPigors' 1st Complaint asserted a number of claims\u2026\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK (Expanded + Embedded Triggers):\r\nEvery listed cause of action was grounded in Michigan statutory law, direct documentation, and verified harm. These were not speculative claims \u2014 they included:\r\n\r\nBreach of Contract \u2013 Rent increases beyond lease terms in violation of MCL 554.633 and Truth in Renting Act.\r\n\r\nFraudulent Misrepresentation \u2013 Charging under a lease that expired, using dissolved LLCs, violating MCL 445.903(1)(cc), (s), (z).\r\n\r\nConsumer Protection Act Violations \u2013 Material deception, bait-and-switch leasing, undisclosed administrative fees.\r\n\r\nRetaliatory Conduct \u2013 Filing evictions during open EGLE complaints and after protected tenant assertions (MCL 600.5775(2)).\r\n\r\nTenant Harassment \u2013 Water shutoff during child presence, hostile service, baseless eviction threats.\r\n\r\nNegligent Property Management \u2013 Raw sewage exposure, health hazards, failure to maintain essential infrastructure (MCL 125.471 et seq.)\r\n\r\nUnlawful Utility Billing \u2013 Charging utilities while failing to repair or properly maintain sewer lines, in breach of lease and health codes.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udca5 These claims are not only legally supportable but mandated for protection of public interest, particularly when Defendant operates as part of a multi-layered national equity syndicate (Alden/Partridge/Homes of America) using artificial LLC separations to shield liability \u2014 a matter now appropriate for veil piercing under Michigan law (see Seasword v Hilti, 449 Mich 542 (1995)).\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b65:\r\n\u201cShady Oaks MHP, LLC filed an Eviction Complaint against Mr. Pigors for non-payment of rent. Exhibit 2.\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nThat complaint was filed under false pretenses, by a landlord already in violation of EGLE sewage regulations, billing during a no-occupancy period, and charging inflated rent without a lease. The \u201cEviction Complaint\u201d was retaliatory, filed while Plaintiff\u2019s complaints to DHHS and EGLE were pending, in violation of MCL 600.5775(2). The complaint failed to disclose that the rent was disputed due to raw sewage backups and fraudulent billing \u2014 conduct constituting both breach of warranty of habitability and retaliatory eviction under Michigan law. Service was defective, ledger fraudulent, and corporate standing unclear due to the use of dissolved LLCs and fictitious names.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b66:\r\n\u201cPigors\u2019 1st Complaint was ultimately dismissed with prejudice by the 60th District Court\u2026\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nFalse frame. The dismissal was not based on merits, but a stipulated conditional settlement under coercive circumstances \u2014 Plaintiff never waived claims arising after the agreement, nor those against non-parties like Homes of America and Alden. Further, the dismissal involved only Shady Oaks MHP, LLC \u2014 not the broader corporate structure now properly before this court. Dismissal in one forum does not bar claims arising post-dismissal or involving distinct defendants and injuries (Winkler v Marist Fathers, 500 Mich 327 (2017)). Defendants\u2019 reliance on this clause to preclude new claims amounts to a res judicata overreach, inapplicable to ongoing and future harms.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b67:\r\n\u201cEviction Complaint ended with a final judgment against Mr. Pigors\u2026 order of eviction entered on June 9, 2025\u2026\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nThis order was secured via procedural suppression, misinformation about lease terms, inflated billing, and concealed sewage violations. Even assuming a valid writ was issued, Plaintiff\u2019s federal rights do not terminate with the issuance of a state writ, and the order itself is under post-judgment challenge (pending PI conversion to damages). Moreover, the eviction was executed during an active utility shutoff and sewage leak in violation of MCL 125.471 and EGLE regulations, rendering enforcement unconscionable and actionable under 42 USC \u00a71983 due to state actor involvement in depriving due process.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b68:\r\n\u201cMr. Pigors did not appeal the dismissal or eviction order.\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nNon-appeal does not bar parallel claims. Plaintiff lawfully chose to pursue relief via separate channels \u2014 including tort and equity in circuit court \u2014 as permitted under MCR 2.203(B) and Michigan law on concurrent remedy doctrine. The claim that Plaintiff \u201cfailed to appeal\u201d is a red herring \u2014 all current causes arise from post-judgment harm, improper corporate concealment, and retaliation for protected activities (filing complaints with HUD, EGLE, and DHHS). Moreover, the scope of appellate review in LT is limited; Plaintiff\u2019s constitutional and property destruction claims properly belong in circuit court.\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b69:\r\n\u201cUnbeknownst to Defendant, Mr. Pigors filed this Complaint on June 13, 2025... many of which were previously asserted...\u201d\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd01 STRIKEBACK:\r\nThis complaint is timely, factually grounded, and independently justiciable. While some harms may overlap with earlier allegations, the operative facts are new, including post-March 2025 retaliation, increased rent, illegal shutoffs, and egregious property destruction during the July 14, 2025 eviction. The defense\u2019s attempt to bar all further claims conflates similarity of harms with legal identity of claims \u2014 an error rejected by Michigan courts in cases of ongoing harm or corporate fraud. See Adair v State of Michigan, 470 Mich 105 (2004), emphasizing claim preclusion applies only where facts, parties, and timing fully align.\r\n\r\n\r\n\ud83d\udd3b Defense \u00b65:\r\n\u201cLLC against Mr. Pigors for non-payment of rent summary proceedings.
